# Two small LCD displays are given, one below the other. In the following, we 
# send I2C messages to them. Each line represents a single message. The address 
# of the upper display is 0x3C, the lower is 0x3D.

# Each line starts with an address, followed by a command (0x00 or 0x40) and 
# parameters.

# The displays are 132 pixels wide and 64 rows high. The rows are divided into 
# pages of eight rows. That is, page 0 corresponds to the first 8 rows of the 
# screen, page 1 to the next 8, and so on up to page 7, which contains the last 
# 8 rows.

# To draw on the display, you must first select a page, and within that a starting 
# column (command 0x00). Once this is set, you send drawing instructions 
# (command 0x40), which, starting from the selected column and moving to the right, 
# set the pixels on the selected page. 

# We are talking about a monochrome display, so one byte can set exactly the 8 
# vertically adjacent pixels of a page.

# Example:
# =========
# Selecting page and column (00): in the parameters you always need to look at the 
# lower 4 bits; this yields the page (0x4) and the column (0x36):

0x3D 00 B4 06 13

# in reality, the 0xB* indicates that we are talking about a page, while 0x0* 
# and 0x1* indicate the low and high bits of column addressing but in the following, 
# the order will always be 0xB*, 0x0*, 0x1*, so you donâ€™t need to worry about this.

# Once the destination is selected, we continute with pixel data (command 40):

0x3D 40 02 02

# starting from column 0x36 on the previously selected page 4, we write 0x02, 0x02 

0x3D 00 B0 06 15
0x3D 40 20 20 20 20 20 20 20 20
